The rationale for choosing 4D SNPs is that they do not cause amino-acid changes and thus, should be under less selective pressure and more reliably reflect population structure and demography<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Fazio, G. et al. Dw2, a new dwarfing locus in apple rootstocks and its relationship to induction of early bearing in apple scions. J. Am. Soc. Hortic. Sci. &#xA;                           139, 87â98 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2782">18</a></sup>. PCA was performed using program EIGENSOFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Patterson, N., Price, A. L. &amp; Reich, D. Population structure and eigenanalysis. PLoS Genet. &#xA;                           2, e190 (2006)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2786">34</a></sup>. A neighbor-joining phylogenetic tree was constructed using MEGA6<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Tamura, K., Stecher, G., Peterson, D., Filipski, A. &amp; Kumar, S. MEGA6: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis version 6.0. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           30, 2725â2729 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2790">35</a></sup> in 1000 bootstrap replicates with pear â<i>Pyrus</i> Ã <i>bretschneideri</i>â as the outgroup. Pear genomic sequence reads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Wu, J. et al. The genome of the pear (Pyrus bretschneideri Rehd.). Genome Res. &#xA;                           23, 396â408 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2801">36</a></sup> were downloaded from the NCBI SRA database (accession no. SRP016889) and aligned to the apple genome v1.0p for SNP calling. Population structure was investigated using STRUCTURE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Hubisz, M. J., Falush, D., Stephens, M. &amp; Pritchard, J. K. Inferring weak population structure with the assistance of sample group information. Mol. Ecol. Resour &#xA;                           9, 1322â1332 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2805">13</a></sup>. To determine the most likely number of ancestral kinships (<i>K</i>) in the apple population, STRUCTURE was run 20 times on 2000 randomly selected 4D SNPs for each <i>K</i> value from 3 to 19. The statistic â<i>âK</i>â, which indicates the change in likelihood of different numbers of clusters, was calculated, and the cluster number with the highest â<i>K</i> value, which indicated the most likely number of clusters in the population, was obtained. We then used the whole set of 4D SNPs to calculate the cluster membership for each accession with 10,000 iterations. According to the phylogenetic and population structure analyses, nine accessions (<i>M. domestica</i>, Dom_15, Dom_29, Dom_32, Dom_34, and Dom_35; other wild species, Kir_01, Ori_01, and Pum_01; <i>M. sylvestris</i>, Syl_10) were positioned into unexpected species groups and thus excluded from downstream population genetics analyses.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Inferring population genetic statistics</h3><p>Nucleotide diversity (<i>Ï</i>) is often used as a measurement of the degree of the genotype variability within a population or species<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Tajima, F. Evolutionary relationship of DNA sequences in finite populations. Genetics &#xA;                           105, 437â460 (1983)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2839">37</a></sup>. Values of <i>Ï</i> were calculated for 10-kb non-overlapping windows across the apple genome with the final set of 7,218,060 SNPs using the BioPerl module PopGen<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Stajich, J. E. &amp; Hahn, M. W. Disentangling the effects of demography and selection in human history. Mol. Biol. Evol. &#xA;                           22, 63â73 (2005)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2846">38</a></sup>.</p><p>Population differentiation is evaluated by the fixation index <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub>
                           <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Nei, M. Analysis of gene diversity in subdivided populations. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA &#xA;                           70, 3321â3323 (1973)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2858">39</a></sup>
                           <sub>.</sub> Pairwise <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub> values were calculated among the eight species groups listed in the Supplementary DataÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#MOESM2">1</a> for the final SNP set using a variance component approach implemented in the R package HIERFSTAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Goudet, J. HIERFSTAT, a package for R to compute and test hierarchical F-statistics. Mol. Ecol. Notes &#xA;                           5, 184â186 (2005)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2873">40</a></sup>. To visualize the 8âÃâ8 pairwise <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub> matrix, multidimensional scaling (MDS) was performed using an R function <i>cmdscale</i> to transfer <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub> values into two dimensional values for plotting. To test the accuracy of this MDS visualization, the Spearman rank-sum correlation <i>Ï</i> was calculated between Euclidean distances between all pairs of values in the MDS plot and the corresponding <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub> values. SNPs with top 1% <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub> values were identified as highly divergent variations in comparisons between <i>M. domestica</i> and each of the four wild groups, including <i>M. sieversii</i> in Kazakhstan, <i>M. sieversii</i> in Xinjiang, <i>M. sylvestris</i>, and other wild species, as well as between rootstock and scion cultivars. To better reflect selective pressure on nucleotide variants, non-synonymous SNPs were further identified from the highly divergent SNPs with top 1% <i>F</i>
                           <sub>ST</sub> values, and the corresponding genes containing these non-synonymous SNPs were determined.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">LD</h3><p>Correlation coefficient (<i>r</i>
                           <sup>2</sup>) of genotypes was calculated to measure LD level in each of the five groups using Haploview<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Barrett, J. C., Fry, B., Maller, J. &amp; Daly, M. J. Haploview: analysis and visualization of LD and haplotype maps. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           21, 263â265 (2005)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d14168e2937">41</a></sup> with the following parameters: -nogui -minMAF 0.10 -hwcutoff 0.001 -dprime. SNPs within each group were extracted for the analysis. SNPs within 500-kb sliding windows were used to estimate average <i>r</i>
                           <sup><i>2</i></sup> at various physical distance classes, and the LD decay was plotted as a function of the derived average <i>r</i>
                           <sup><i>2</i></sup> and physical distances. Tag SNPs were also identified using Haploview with parameters set as follows: -nogui -minMAF 0.05 -hwcutoff 0.001 -dprime -blockoutput GAB -minGeno 0.8 -pairwiseTagging.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Inferring-derived alleles</h3><p>To evaluate whether major alleles of <i>M. domestica</i> (<i>Dom</i>) are derived from those of <i>M. sieversii</i> in Kazakhstan (<i>Sie_K</i>) or <i>M. sylvestris</i> (<i>Syl</i>), the entire genome was scanned using SNPs with MAF â¥5% and missing rate per site â¤10%. First, allele frequency per site was computed in each species group and the allele with the frequency &gt;0.6 was assigned as the major allele. For each site, we considered the major allele in <i>Sie_K</i> as the ancestral allele in <i>Dom</i> if these two groups share consistent major alleles; similarly, <i>Syl</i> was considered as the allelic ancestor for <i>Dom</i> when they had the same major alleles. For each non-overlapping 100-kb window, if the count of ancestral alleles as <i>Sie_K</i> was greater than two times of that as <i>Syl</i> and the total SNP count was larger than five, we regarded this region as being derived from <i>Sie_K</i>; similarly, if the ancestral-allele count ratio between <i>Syl</i> and <i>Sie_K</i> was larger than two and the window contained more than five SNPs, we considered this window as originating from <i>Syl</i>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Identification of selective sweeps</h3><p>Selective sweeps across the genome were identified using a XP-CLR method that models the allele frequency spectrum to search for signals of differentiation between two populations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Chen, H., Patterson, N. &amp; Reich, D. Population differentiation as a test for selective sweeps. Genome Res. &#xA;                           20, 393â402 (2010)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3022">42</a></sup>, following previous studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Hufford, M. B. et al. Comparative population genomics of maize domestication and improvement. Nat. Genet. &#xA;                           44, 808â811 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3026">43</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Xie, W. et al. Breeding signatures of rice improvement revealed by a genomic variation map from a large germplasm collection. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA &#xA;                           112, E5411âE5419 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3029">44</a></sup> with modifications. Briefly, selection screening was performed in two contrasts: <i>M. domestica</i> vs. <i>M. sieversii</i> in Kazakhstan for initial domestication (<i>Dom_SieK</i>) and <i>M. domestica</i> vs. <i>M. sylvestris</i> for introgressive domestication (<i>Dom_Syl</i>). Genetic distances between adjacent SNPs were calculated according to their physical distances in a widely used genetic map reported with the apple reference genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Velasco, R. et al. The genome of the domesticated apple (Malus x domestica Borkh.). Nat. Genet. &#xA;                           42, 833â839 (2010)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3052">12</a></sup>. Parameters â-w1 0.0005 100 100 -p0 0.7â were adopted to run the program for each chromosome, allowing XP-CLR scores to be calculated for each 100-bp region using unphased SNPs with correlation level at 0.7 and no more than 100 SNPs per window (in size of 0.05âcM). The XP-CLR scores per 100âbp were averaged across non-overlapping 10-kb windows on each chromosome. Adjacent 10-kb windows with an average XP-CLR score no less than 80% of the genome-wide average XP-CLR score were joined as putative selective regions, which were further merged together if two regions were separated by only one low-score 10-kb window. The maximum of window-wise average XP-CLR scores in a merged region was assigned as the region-wise XP-CLR score. Merged regions with top 10% of region-wise XP-CLR scores were considered as candidate selective sweeps. To improve the prediction accuracy, only candidate selective sweeps having top 50% of <i>Ï</i> ratios between the ancestral and domesticated species were kept.</p><p>Genes in the candidate selective sweeps were grouped by their physical locations into each 1-Mb non-overlapping segments throughout the genome. Adjacent segments and segments separated by no more than 1-Mb were merged together, while segments containing no more than five genes were discarded. GO term enrichment analyses were conducted for genes in each merged segment along the genome using GO::TermFinder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Boyle, E. I. et al. GO::TermFinder--open source software for accessing Gene Ontology information and finding significantly enriched Gene Ontology terms associated with a list of genes. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           20, 3710â3715 (2004)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3062">45</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Genome-wide association study</h3><p>The USDA-GRIN database archives phenotypic observations for 105 different traits in 4123 apple accessions from 1995 to 2014 (<a href="https://npgsweb.ars-grin.gov/gringlobal/cropdetail.aspx?type=descriptor&amp;id=115">https://npgsweb.ars-grin.gov/gringlobal/cropdetail.aspx?type=descriptor&amp;id=115</a>). The phenotypic scores of fruit flavor, weight, width, length, flesh firmness, skin color, and soluble solid content were downloaded for 66 out of the 70 accessions from USDA-ARS that are included in the USDA-GRIN database. Phenotype scores recorded in multiple years for a particular accession were screened to exclude outliers (more than 1.5 times the interquartile range below the first quartile or above the third quartile) and then averaged across the years. Tukeyâs HSD mean separation tests were conducted to analyze these phenotypes in pairwise comparisons between <i>M. domestica</i>, <i>M. sieversii</i> in Kazakhstan, and <i>M. sylvestris</i>.</p><p>Phenotypic data of skin color was used for the association study. To improve phenotyping of fruit skin color, we manually examined fruit pictures in the USDA-GRIN database and assigned a score of fruit skin color for each accession using the following scoring system: 0, <i>green</i>; 1, <i>yellow</i>; 2, <i>light red</i> (<i>green base</i> with <i>pink-red</i> area and/or stripes less than half of the fruit); 3, <i>medium red</i> (<i>green-yellow</i> base with blush more than half of the fruit); 4, <i>red</i> (without <i>green</i> or <i>yellow base</i>); 5, <i>dark red</i>. Same was done on 13 accessions collected from China (Supplementary TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#MOESM1">3</a>). The final set SNPs were filtered by keeping those with missing rate â¤10%, MAF â¥5%, SNP calling rate per accession â¥80%, and <i>P</i> value of Hardy-Weinberg equilibrium test â¤0.001. The resulting SNPs were used to perform GWAS for fruit skin color using a linear mixed model (LMM) implemented in the FaST-LMM program<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Lippert, C. et al. FaST linear mixed models for genome-wide association studies. Nat. Methods &#xA;                           8, 833â835 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3134">46</a></sup>. Raw <i>P</i> values were adjusted for multiple testing using the Benjamini-Hochberg procedure<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Benjamini, Y. &amp; Hochberg, Y. Controlling the false discovery rate: a practical and powerful approach to multiple testing. J. R. Stat. Soc. B &#xA;                           57, 289â300 (1995)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3141">47</a></sup> and a significant association was based on a threshold of false discovery rate of 0.1 (corresponding to raw <i>P</i> value of 3.03âÃâ10<sup>â6</sup>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">RNA-seq data generation and gene expression analysis</h3><p>Fruit samples were taken at five stages of fruit development from the apple cultivar âGreensleevesâ: 18 days after bloom (DAB) (active cell division), 37 DAB (the end of cell division), 67 DAB (rapid cell expansion), 90 DAB (rapid cell expansion), and 132 DAB (ripening). Three biological replicates were collected for each stage. Fresh tissues were immediately frozen in liquid nitrogen and ground to fine powder. Total RNA was extracted using the QIAGEN RNeasy Plant Mini Kit (Qiagen, USA) followed by treatment with RNase-free DNase I (Promega, USA) according to the manufacturersâ protocols. Strand-specific Illumina RNA-Seq libraries were constructed following the protocol described in Zhong et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Zhong, S. et al. High-throughput Illumina strand-specific RNA sequencing library preparation. Cold Spring Harb. Protoc. &#xA;                           2011, 940â949 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3159">48</a></sup> and sequenced on the Illumina HiSeq 2000 system using single-end 51-bp mode. Around 20â50 million reads were generated for each of the 15 libraries. Raw reads were first processed to remove adapter and low-quality sequences using Trimmomatic<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Bolger, A. M., Lohse, M. &amp; Usadel, B. Trimmomatic: a flexible trimmer for Illumina sequence data. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           30, 2114â2120 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3163">31</a></sup>. Reads shorter than 40âbp after trimming were discarded. The resulting reads were then aligned to the ribosomal RNA database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Quast, C. et al. The SILVA ribosomal RNA gene database project: improved data processing and web-based tools. Nucleic Acids Res. &#xA;                           41, D590âD596 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3167">49</a></sup> using Bowtie<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Langmead, B., Trapnell, C., Pop, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Ultrafast and memory-efficient alignment of short DNA sequences to the human genome. Genome Biol. &#xA;                           10, R25 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3171">50</a></sup>, allowing up to three mismatches. The aligned reads were discarded and the remaining reads were aligned to the apple genome (v1.0) using HISAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Kim, D., Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat. Methods &#xA;                           12, 357â360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3175">51</a></sup>. Raw counts for each apple gene were derived from the read alignments and normalized to reads per kilobase of exon model per million mapped reads (RPKM). Differential expression analyses were performed using edgeR<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Robinson, M. D., McCarthy, D. J. &amp; Smyth, G. K. edgeR: a Bioconductor package for differential expression analysis of digital gene expression data. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           26, 139â140 (2010)." href="/articles/s41467-017-00336-7#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d14168e3180">52</a></sup>. Genes with adjusted <i>P</i> values less than 0.01, expression changes of at least twofold, and expression levels of at least 1 RPKM in at least one of the five stages were identified as differentially expressed genes during fruit development.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Data availability</h3><p>Sequence reads of genome and transcriptome resequencing have been deposited into the NCBI sequence read archive under accessions SRP075497 and SRP102350, respectively. SNP data sets can be accessed at <a href="ftp://bioinfo.bti.cornell.edu/pub/Apple_SNP/">ftp://bioinfo.bti.cornell.edu/pub/Apple_SNP/</a>.</p></div></div></section>
